[01/08/22, 14:56:07] Aditya Mahale (dy ): Aim: 
The aim of this case study is to design and develop a database maintaining records of different books, staff members, walk-in readers, students and issued books in a library. Records include unique ISBN of books, title, publisher, category, etc. and information about the readers will include name, address, student id, etc. Information about available and borrowed books, as well as fines will also be shown.

Description:
Readers can read the books or issue them as per their requirement and availability. Students can access information about books to browse them by category or check inventory if it‚Äôs available for rental. Staff members can authorize issuing of books to students and keep track of the books issued date for its return and also to charge late fees if book is returned post the due date. Track of active student memberships for the library can be recorded as well.

Table Description:
Following are the tables along with constraints used in Library Management database.
1.	Book_List: This table will consist of details about the books in the library. The information stored in it will include a unique ISBN, title of the book, category, author, publisher, availability and its price for issuing. 
                                                                                   
Constraint: ISBN should be unique for each book.

2.	Staff_List: This table will consist of details about the working staff of the library. The information stored in it includes a unique staff id, name of staff, address and time of their shift.

Constraint: Staff id should be unique for each staff member.

3.	Issued_Books: This table will consist of details about the books currently in circulation or issued. It will store information like ISBN, title of book, student id and name of borrower, return date, etc.

Constraint: ISBN and title of book should exist in Book_List table.

4.	Student_Memberships: This table will consist of details about the existing memberships of students in the library. The information stored in it includes name and student id, date of acquiring membership, duration and price paid.

Constraint: Student id should be unique and should exist in Students_Info table.

5.	Students_Info: This table will consist of details about the students entering the library. The information stored in it includes name of student, student id, entry and exit time, etc.

Constraint: Student id should be unique.

6.	Fines_Dues: This table will consist of details about any existing fines for late or no returning of books for the students. It will include the borrower details, due date, return date, ISBN and title of book and amount of the fine with its status.  

Relational Database Schema:
The relational database sc

[03/10/22, 14:38:20] Aditya Mahale (dy ): CREATE TABLE Book_List
(
               isbn NUMERIC PRIMARY KEY,
              title VARCHAR(60) UNIQUE,
           category VARCHAR(20) NOT NULL,
             author VARCHAR(20) NOT NULL,
          publisher VARCHAR(20) NOT NULL,
  quantity_in_stock NUMERIC     NOT NULL,
        issue_price NUMERIC     CHECK(issue_price<300)
);

CREATE TABLE Issued_Books
(
          isbn NUMERIC,
         title VARCHAR(60),
    student_id NUMERIC PRIMARY KEY,
  student_name VARCHAR(40),
      due_date VARCHAR(20),
    CONSTRAINT RT_BOOK
       FOREIGN KEY(isbn)
    REFERENCES Book_List(isbn)
);

>Creating tables;
CREATE TABLE Book_List 
( 
                 isbn NUMERIC, 
                title VARCHAR(60), 
             category VARCHAR(20), 
               author VARCHAR(20), 
            publisher VARCHAR(20), 
    quantity_in_stock NUMERIC, 
          issue_price NUMERIC
);

CREATE TABLE Issued_Books 
( 
            isbn NUMERIC, 
           title VARCHAR(60), 
      student_id NUMERIC, 
    student_name VARCHAR(40), 
        due_date VARCHAR(20)
); 

CREATE TABLE Library_Staff 
( 
         staff_id NUMERIC, 
       staff_name VARCHAR(30), 
        staff_phn NUMERIC(10), 
    time_of_shift VARCHAR(20) 
);

CREATE TABLE Student_Info 
( 
       student_id NUMERIC, 
     student_name VARCHAR(30), 
      student_phn NUMERIC(10), 
    ms_start_date VARCHAR(20), 
      ms_end_date VARCHAR(20) 
);

CREATE TABLE Fines_Dues 
( 
      student_id NUMERIC, 
    student_name VARCHAR(30), 
           title VARCHAR(30), 
            isbn NUMERIC, 
     return_date VARCHAR(20), 
        due_date VARCHAR(20) 
);

DESC Book_List;
DESC Issued_Books;
DESC Library_Staff;
DESC Student_Info;
DESC Fines_Dues;

>Using all five constraint types in example;
CREATE TABLE Book_List
(
                 isbn NUMERIC PRIMARY KEY,
                title VARCHAR(60) UNIQUE,
             category VARCHAR(20),
               author VARCHAR(20) NOT NULL,
            publisher VARCHAR(20),
    quantity_in_stock NUMERIC,
          issue_price NUMERIC CHECK(issue_price<300)
);

CREATE TABLE Issued_Books
(
            isbn NUMERIC,
           title VARCHAR(60),
      student_id NUMERIC PRIMARY KEY,
    student_name VARCHAR(60) NOT NULL,
        due_date VARCHAR(20),
    CONSTRAINT RT_BOOK
    FOREIGN KEY(isbn)
    REFERENCES Book_List(isbn)
);

DESC Book_List;
DESC Issued_Books;

>Examples of string operations;
SELECT * FROM Book_List WHERE author LIKE 'J%';

SELECT * FROM Book_List WHERE author LIKE 'B_%_%';

SELECT * FROM Book_List WHERE publisher LIKE 'P%n';

SELECT * FROM Book_List WHERE author NOT LIKE 'J%';

SELECT * FROM Book_List WHERE publisher LIKE '%n';

SELECT * FROM Book_List WHERE category LIKE '%om%';

SELECT * FROM Book_List WHERE title LIKE '_a%';

	$firstName = $_POST['firstName'];
	$lastName = $_POST['lastName'];
	$gender = $_POST['gender'];
	$email = $_POST['email'];
	$password = $_POST['password'];
	$number = $_POST['number'];

	// Database connection
	$conn = new mysqli('localhost','root','','test');
	if($conn->connect_error){
		echo "$conn->connect_error";
		die("Connection Failed : ". $conn->connect_error);
	} else {
		$stmt = $conn->prepare("insert into registration(firstName, lastName, gender, email, password, number) values(?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?)");
		$stmt->bind_param("sssssi", $firstName, $lastName, $gender, $email, $password, $number);
		$execval = $stmt->execute();
		echo $execval;
		echo "Registration successfully...";
		$stmt->close();
		$conn->close();
	}

[09/11/22, 14:03:44] Prathamesh Tripathi: Influence of compression rate on initial success of resuscitation and 24 hour survival after prolonged manual cardiopulmonary resuscitation in dogs.

MICHAEL P Feneley, GEORGE W Maier, KARL B Kern, J WILLIAM Gaynor, SA Gall Jr, ARTHUR B Sanders, K Raessler, LH Muhlbaier, J Scott Rankin, GA Ewy
Circulation 77 (1), 240-250, 1988
The influence of chest compression rate on initial resuscitation success and 24 hr survival after prolonged manual cardiopulmonary resuscitation (CPR) was investigated in 26 morphine-anesthetized dogs (17 to 30 kg). After placement of aortic and right atrial micromanometers and induction of ventricular fibrillation, manual CPR was commenced immediately and continued for 30 min. One group of 13 dogs underwent manual CPR at a compression rate of 60/min, and the other group at a rate of 120/min. The compression durations in the two groups were not significantly different (51.7 +/- 1.8% at 60/min vs 51.6 +/- 1.9% at 120/min). No drugs other than sodium bicarbonate were administered during CPR. A maximum of three attempts was permitted to defibrillate the heart. Successfully defibrillated animals were followed for 24 hr, during which time no treatment, other than naloxone, was given to reverse the effects of morphine. Arterial blood pH, PCO2, and PO2 were not significantly different in the two groups throughout the CPR period. When compared with the compression rate of 60/min, the compression rate of 120/min produced more successfully defibrillated animals (12/13 at 120/min vs 2/13 at 60/min, p less than .002) and more 24 hr survivors (8/13 at 120/min vs 2/13 at 60/min, p less than .03). All 24 hr survivors were conscious and able to sit, stand, and drink normally. One 24 hr survivor in each group had difficulty walking. Improved survival with the high-rate compression technique was consistent with the significantly higher mean aortic (systolic and diastolic) and coronary perfusion pressures attained with high-rate compressions (all p less than .002). Although the clinical applicability of these findings has yet to be demonstrated, they provide empirical support for the recent decision to increase the chest compression rate for manual CPR recommended by the American Heart Association, and indicate that the hemodynamic and survival benefits of faster compression rates in this experimental preparation were not dependent on covariant alterations in compression duration.

[16/11/22, 13:37:26] Aditya Mahale (dy ): Nature Tourism Constraints: A Cross-Activity Comparison
[16/11/22, 13:37:34] Aditya Mahale (dy ): by google scholar
[16/11/22, 13:37:48] Aditya Mahale (dy ): Abstract
The purpose of this paper is to examine the reasons that keep individuals from participating in three nature-based tourism activities registering limited growth in contrast with the increasing popularity of tourism in general. The three-dimensional leisure constraints model was used as the theoretical framework for the study. The sample consisted of nature enthusiasts from several US states who showed an interest in nature tourism but did not participate in the selected activities during the last two years. Confirmatory factor analysis partially supported the three-dimensional model across the activities. Repeated measures comparisons showed that the importance of leisure constraints varied across them within the same group of individuals.

[16/11/22, 13:41:16] Aditya Mahale (dy ): Survival Manual based on the Army Field Manual 21-76 - fully working offline. It
contains info on how to make fire, build a shelter, find food, heal and other
useful content in a case of emergency.

But it does not have to be used in emergency situations only - it can be also
useful for trips to the outdoors, hiking, camping, learning about nature and
yourself truly. This is not only fun, but you can also train skills (make fire,
build shelter, ..) you might need in a catastrophy. Some things work best with
practice in a relaxed environment - then you also have time for some
experiments.

[02/02/23, 10:41:04] Aditya Mahale (dy ): #include<stdio.h>
#include<conio.h>

void InsertionSort(int array[],int size);

void main()
{
    int a[10],n,i;
    clrscr();
    printf("Enter size of array: ");
    scanf("%d",&n);
    printf("Enter array elements:\n");
    for(i=0;i<n;i++)
    {
	scanf("%d",&a[i]);
    }
    InsertionSort(a,n);
    printf("Sorted array: ");
    for(i=0;i<n;i++)
    {
	printf("%d ",a[i]);
    }
}

void InsertionSort(int array[],int size)
{
    for(int step=1;step<size;step++)
    {
	int key=array[step];
	int j=step-1;

	while(key<array[j] && j>=0)
	{
	    array[j+1]=array[j];
	    --j;
	}
	array[j+1]=key;
    }
}

[02/02/23, 10:41:42] Aditya Mahale (dy ): #include<stdio.h>
#include<conio.h>

int Bsearch(int a[],int start,int end,int key);

void main()
{
    clrscr();
    int i,n,key,a[10];

    printf("Enter size of array: ");
    scanf("%d",&n);

    printf("Enter array elements:\n");
    for(i=0;i<n;i++)
    {
	scanf("%d",&a[i]);
    }

    printf("\nEnter element to be searched: ");
    scanf("%d",&key);

    int pos=Bsearch(a,0,n,key);
    if(pos==-1)
    {
	printf("Element not found");
    }
    else
    {
	printf("Element found at index %d",pos);
    }
}

int Bsearch(int a[],int start,int end,int key)
{
    if(end>=start)
    {
	int mid=(start+end)/2;
	if(key==a[mid])
	{
	    return mid;
	}
	else if(key<a[mid])
	{
	    return Bsearch(a,start,mid-1,key);
	}
	else if(key>a[mid])
	{
	    return Bsearch(a,mid+1,end,key);
	}
    }
    return -1;
}

[02/02/23, 10:42:26] Aditya Mahale (dy ): #include<stdio.h>
void swap(int *xp, int *yp)
{int temp = *xp;
	*xp = *yp;
	*yp = temp;}
void selectionSort(int arr[], int n)
{int i, j, min_idx;
    for (i = 0; i < n-1; i++)
	{min_idx = i;
		for (j = i+1; j < n; j++)
		if (arr[j] < arr[min_idx])
			min_idx = j;
          if(min_idx != i)
			swap(&arr[min_idx], &arr[i]);}}
void printArray(int arr[], int size)
{ int i;
	for (i=0; i < size; i++)
		printf("%d ", arr[i]);
	printf("\n");}
int main()
{printf("Enter the array elements = \n");
	int arr[5];
	for(int i = 0;i<5 ;i++){
	scanf("%d", &arr[i]);}
	int n = sizeof(arr)/sizeof(arr[0]);
	selectionSort(arr, n);
	printf("Sorted array: \n");
	printArray(arr, n);
	return 0;}

[13/07/23, 09:17:01] Prathamesh Tripathi: There are several essential employment skills that are highly valued by employers. These skills can vary depending on the specific job or industry, but some commonly mentioned essential employment skills include:

Communication[1]: Effective communication is crucial in almost any job. It involves the ability to convey information clearly, listen actively, and express oneself both verbally and in writing.

Collaboration and teamwork[1]: Many jobs require working with others to achieve common goals. Being able to collaborate effectively, contribute to a team, and work cooperatively with colleagues is highly valued by employers.

Problem-solving and critical thinking[1][2]: Employers are looking for individuals who can analyze problems, identify solutions, and make informed decisions. Being able to think critically and creatively and come up with innovative solutions is a valuable skill in the workplace.
[13/07/23, 09:17:01] Prathamesh Tripathi: Adaptability and flexibility[1]: In a rapidly changing work environment, employers value individuals who can adapt quickly to new situations and handle multiple tasks efficiently. Being flexible and open to learning new things is an essential skill for career success.

Time management and organization[1]: Being able to manage one's time effectively, prioritize tasks, and stay organized is crucial in meeting deadlines and being productive in the workplace.

Leadership skills[1]: Regardless of the position, having leadership skills is valuable in demonstrating initiative, taking responsibility, and influencing others positively.

Technical and digital literacy[1]: With the increasing reliance on technology in the modern workplace, having proficiency in relevant technical skills and being digitally literate is important in many jobs.
[13/07/23, 09:17:01] Prathamesh Tripathi: Communication: Effective communication involves not only expressing yourself clearly but also actively listening, being empathetic, and adjusting your communication style to the needs of others.

Emotional Intelligence: Emotional intelligence refers to the ability to recognize and understand your own emotions and those of others. It involves managing emotions, showing empathy, and navigating relationships effectively.

Adaptability: Being adaptable means being open to change, able to adjust to new situations, and find creative solutions. It is about being flexible, resilient, and embracing continuous learning.

Teamwork and Collaboration: Working well with others is essential for success in many roles. This skill includes being cooperative, respectful, and contributing positively to a team's dynamics.

Problem-Solving: The ability to approach challenges and find effective solutions is highly valued. Problem-solving skills involve critical thinking, analytical reasoning, creativity, and resourcefulness.
[13/07/23, 09:17:01] Prathamesh Tripathi: Leadership: Leadership skills go beyond formal leadership roles. It includes taking initiative, motivating others, and contributing to the success of a team or organization.

Time Management: Being able to effectively manage time helps prioritize tasks, meet deadlines, and improve overall productivity. This skill involves planning, organizing, and setting realistic goals.

Empathy: Empathy is the ability to understand and share the feelings and perspectives of others. It involves active listening, showing compassion, and being able to connect with colleagues or clients on a deeper level.

Conflict Resolution: Conflict is inevitable in any work environment. The ability to resolve conflicts in a constructive and fair manner is crucial for maintaining positive relationships and productivity.

Professionalism: Demonstrating professionalism involves having a positive attitude, being reliable, punctual, and maintaining high ethical standards. It includes taking accountability for one's actions and displaying integrity.
